<span id="freeTextContainer13921590087837928915">No...just no. I keep on editing this review, to try and explain, how vile and sad this type of imagination is for anyone to have, let alone publish. This was so painful to get through, the only reason I gave this 1 star, is because I applaud it for the fact that it made me feel severely uncomfortable. This must be amazing for a severely depressed goth/emo suicidal teenager dreaming of being someones blood donor, convinced no one has a shittier life than theirs , screaming for attention, dwelling</span>
  <span id="freeText13921590087837928915" style="display:none">No...just no. I keep on editing this review, to try and explain, how vile and sad this type of imagination is for anyone to have, let alone publish. This was so painful to get through, the only reason I gave this 1 star, is because I applaud it for the fact that it made me feel severely uncomfortable. This must be amazing for a severely depressed goth/emo suicidal teenager dreaming of being someones blood donor, convinced no one has a shittier life than theirs , screaming for attention, dwelling in self pity. I'm a sucker for weirdness, but this was weird in all the emotionally unstable, dirty, wrong ways. I'll go rinse my brain with children's songs now.<br /><br />Some things, should indicate therapy. This is one of those things. I'd think the author has some sort of mental instability that borders on a severely deranged. It is certainly a form of disordered thinking. I just wish she would have written a book about how to get help for it, instead of encouraging other f#cked up teenagers to think the same.<br /><br />And by reading the reviews, said teenagers never grew up either * Facepalm*</span>
  <a data-text-id="13921590087837928915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3218362331" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3218362331" />
    <a title="Briar Ripley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/93135750-briar-ripley"><img alt="Briar Ripley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549315759p2/93135750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3218362331?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Briar Ripley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Briar Ripley" href="/user/show/93135750-briar-ripley">Briar Ripley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3218362331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6707150967176635492">Does it really surprise anyone that this was one of my very favorite novels when I was 14-16 years old? Anyone? Anyone? No?<br/><br/>Well, it was. In re-reading it, I can appreciate its tremendous influence on me more than ever: my particular taste in gory, squalid, decadent, yet emotional, romantic, and character-driven horror fiction; my own writing style; even my sense of myself as a queer transmasculine person stem in large part from encountering LOST SOULS (and subsequently the rest of Brite's late 8</span>
  <span id="freeText6707150967176635492" style="display:none">Does it really surprise anyone that this was one of my very favorite novels when I was 14-16 years old? Anyone? Anyone? No?<br /><br />Well, it was. In re-reading it, I can appreciate its tremendous influence on me more than ever: my particular taste in gory, squalid, decadent, yet emotional, romantic, and character-driven horror fiction; my own writing style; even my sense of myself as a queer transmasculine person stem in large part from encountering LOST SOULS (and subsequently the rest of Brite's late 80s- early 90s fiction) at a formative age. Brite was in his early 20s when he wrote LOST SOULS, and re-reading it, that's very obvious. Not because it's a clumsily written book: I still think the language is gorgeous, unabashed in its floridity, great at rendering grotesque characters and situations in a way that's both upsetting and alluring. It's just that the emotional timbre and narrative voice of the story is overwrought in a particularly adolescent way. This generally works, as the principal characters are either under the age of 23, or are vampires in a state of perpetual arrested development both physical and emotional/moral/cognitive. It also helps that Brite has a wry self-awareness about some of the more melodramatic and self-aggrandizing ways his characters think about themselves and their situations. Nothing's suburban misfit angst at the beginning of the novel, in particular, is treated with great sympathy but also poked fun at (and it stands in clear contrast to the genuinely traumatic, tragic, and violent situations he encounters later in the story). Still, there are moments where as an adult reader I lose patience with the sincere purple-prose romanticization of nihilistic hedonism and self-destruction, and with LOST SOULS' frequently self-conscious Edginess (some of which, like the way it handles Steve's rape of Ann and a villain's casual N-word dropping towards the beginning, has really, *really* not aged well). <br /><br />The novel has a bit of a misogyny problem in its treatment of female characters, too, though I will defend its use of monstrous, deadly vampire pregnancy as a repeated plot device. Brite is a trans man, and in that motif I see a very emotionally frank metaphorical handling of the particular horror pregnancy holds for many transmasculine people. I think it is difficult for people of other gender experiences to fully understand that horror; in my opinion, monstrous and deadly pregnancy signifies something different when used by a trans male writer than it does when used by a cis male writer, or by a female writer. That said, the general lack of focus on LOST SOULS' female characters, despite their importance as plot devices, and its inconsistent, victim-blaming, often shallow depiction of Ann, are real faults of the novel.<br /><br />On the other hand, a lot of Brite's observations on abusive and dysfunctional interpersonal dynamics are keen and insightful. Nothing's willingness to submit to abuse, manipulation, and sexual exploitation-- and eventually to murder-- if it means he can finally secure a sense of acceptance, love, and belonging rings terribly true. Various characters' frantic, self-pitying self-justifications for their acts of violence, cruelty, and cowardice ring true as well. Ghost and Steve's intense, co-dependent homoerotic friendship is alternately chilling, frustrating, sexy, and kind of heartwarming. And I would submit that Ghost (for me, anyway) offers a still-striking and unusual portrayal of what a gentle, non-toxic masculinity could look like.<br /><br />Like BLACK AMBROSIA, LOST SOULS strikes an excellent balance between the sympathetic vampire, the seductive vampire, and the monstrous/evil vampire; its creatures of the night are all three. Also like BLACK AMBROSIA, its vampires are transients who live filthy, marginal lives working odd jobs or living on the money they scavenge from their victims. I maintain that this makes a lot more sense as a vampiric lifestyle than an aristocratic existence of cultured splendor in a Gothic mansion or castle-- at least, if you're using the vampire as a metaphor for addiction, queerness, marginality, and destructive relationships rather than as a metaphor for the way the rich exploit the poor and working classes. The gore scenes are also great here, with eroticism slowly sliding or abruptly diving into grand guignol splatterpunk bloodbaths. If nothing else, LOST SOULS more than holds up as a *vampire* novel-- I'd say it remains one of the better ones out there!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6707150967176635492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2861521851" />
    <a title="Devann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4135942-devann"><img alt="Devann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603225622p2/4135942.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2861521851?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Devann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Devann" href="/user/show/4135942-devann">Devann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4135942-devann?shelf=z-19-wheelathon-iv">z-19-wheelathon-iv</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4135942-devann?shelf=c-dl">c-dl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4135942-devann?shelf=sg-lgbtia">sg-lgbtia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4135942-devann?shelf=g-horror">g-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4135942-devann?shelf=cr-morally-gray">cr-morally-gray</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4135942-devann?shelf=3-5-star">3-5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4135942-devann?shelf=cr-vamps-weres-zombies">cr-vamps-weres-zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4135942-devann?shelf=a-adult">a-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2861521851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6315165515923104878"><i>I can take pain. It will pass. And if I choose to return and take my pain out of your hide, I will. Or, if you like, I’ll shove my tongue down your throat and corrupt you with my spit. Or, if you prefer, I’ll unzip your skin and kiss you with your own heart-blood on my lips. Are you tempted yet?</i><br/><br/>actual rating: 3.5<br/><br/>This ...was certainly a time. It definitely captures that ~gothic teenage angst~ feeling very well, and although at 29 years old I find it all more than a bit ridiculous I would have bee</span>
  <span id="freeText6315165515923104878" style="display:none"><i>I can take pain. It will pass. And if I choose to return and take my pain out of your hide, I will. Or, if you like, I’ll shove my tongue down your throat and corrupt you with my spit. Or, if you prefer, I’ll unzip your skin and kiss you with your own heart-blood on my lips. Are you tempted yet?</i><br /><br />actual rating: 3.5<br /><br />This ...was certainly a time. It definitely captures that ~gothic teenage angst~ feeling very well, and although at 29 years old I find it all more than a bit ridiculous I would have been SO into this when I was 16. While it is very obvious that Brite wrote this while still a teenager himself it is actually pretty well written, if a bit over the top much of the time. There is a lot of messed up stuff in here so I'll do my best to give you a trigger warning list - I don't think I could have read this if I hadn't known all of it beforehand - but I do want to to single out one thing first. <br /><br />While I enjoyed this overall, the reason I rounded it down is because I just cannot in good conscience rate a book more than 3 stars if every single woman in it gets raped and dies giving birth. That might seem hypocritical since I gave Exquisite Corpse 4 stars and there were no women in that at all, but I can see why there would not be women in a book that uses murder as a metaphor for the AIDS crisis and would honestly rather women were not present at all than to be included to be very minor characters and be treated the way they were here.<br /><br />Other than the whole 'three entire female characters, only one of whom is actually alive in the present timeline or for more than a few pages, who are all raped and die giving birth to vampire babies because wow what a hot take right there' mess, there is also parent/child incest [between a father and teenage daughter that comes with the added gross factor of her being the one to 'seduce' him and then also between a father and teenage son who decide that it's fine since they're vampires and that makes it not count I guess?] as well as just a lot of underage sex in general [the main character is 15] and a woman who is raped by her ex-boyfriend after she breaks up with him. <br /><br />I don't necessarily know WHY I liked this book so much considering all of the above, but I guess sometimes it is interesting to think of the [generally misguided] attitudes that you had as a teenager and become a bit nostalgic for that time in your life even though I think I would genuinely slap my teenage self if I ever met her lol. This is definitely something for the edgy teenage goth crowd, and also probably for people who think that Anne Rice isn't messed up or explicit enough ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6315165515923104878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1945387996" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1945387996" />
    <a title="Bryndís" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51909730-brynd-s"><img alt="Bryndís" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453675907p2/51909730.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1945387996?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2018</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1891586966" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1891586966" />
    <a title="Tobin Elliott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/624440-tobin-elliott"><img alt="Tobin Elliott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583699239p2/624440.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1891586966?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tobin Elliott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tobin Elliott" href="/user/show/624440-tobin-elliott">Tobin Elliott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385308755" href="/book/show/102141.Lost_Souls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/624440-tobin-elliott?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/624440-tobin-elliott?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/624440-tobin-elliott?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1891586966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4660661369631866431">Twenty-five years after my first reading, I decided to dive back into this one again. I remember little about the first read other than not being that impressed and not knowing what to think about all that "gay stuff" that I read.<br/><br/>All this time later, I like to think I'm more mature and understanding with the "gay stuff"...and no, I don't call it that anymore. And this time around, I <i>was</i> impressed with what I read.<br/><br/>For the sake of clarity, though I know Poppy Z. Brite, female at the time of the re</span>
  <span id="freeText4660661369631866431" style="display:none">Twenty-five years after my first reading, I decided to dive back into this one again. I remember little about the first read other than not being that impressed and not knowing what to think about all that "gay stuff" that I read.<br /><br />All this time later, I like to think I'm more mature and understanding with the "gay stuff"...and no, I don't call it that anymore. And this time around, I <i>was</i> impressed with what I read.<br /><br />For the sake of clarity, though I know Poppy Z. Brite, female at the time of the release of this novel, is now Billy Martin and prefers masculine tags, I'm going to stick with "she" for the review, as it does refer to Martin 25 years earlier.<br /><br />To be clear, the novel is not without its faults, but, if what I've read is true and this story was written when Brite was just 19, then it's almost impossible for it not to have some awkward moments.<br /><br />It is, of course, much less shocking that it would have been upon its release, but I still applaud Brite for taking it in some of the directions she did. I can't think of another novel that so perfectly captures the vacuous emptiness of the Eighties and the directionless morbidity of America's youth at the time. Tying in the music of Bowie, Bauhaus, and the Cure, and the poetry of Dylan Thomas, it helped set the mood and the tone for the story.<br /><br />As others have mentioned, there's little plot, at times feeling like an Eighties vampiric version of Kerouac's <i>On The Road</i>. But if I had to compare it to any other works, I'd say it's a mashup of the New Orleans atmosphere of Anne Rice, without all the boring shit (which is most of Anne Rice), the carnal sensuality of Clive Barker, the casual violence of John Skipp and Craig Spector, and the confused, nihilistic youth of S.E. Hinton. That's quite a punch.<br /><br />Could the story have been laid out a bit better? Yes. But overall, the word choice, the ideas, the examination of youth...all of it...gorgeous. The movie <i>The Lost Boys</i> only wishes it had this much depth and soul.<br /><br />Well done.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4660661369631866431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_62899780" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62899780" />
    <a title="Kate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/104823-kate"><img alt="Kate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527527813p2/104823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62899780?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate" href="/user/show/104823-kate">Kate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kate by: </span>
      Novelist
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104823-kate?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104823-kate?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104823-kate?shelf=age-adult">age-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104823-kate?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104823-kate?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62899780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4255786451644418238">I found out about this book from the "Getting Up to Speed in Horror" list on the NoveList database. I'd read or heard of most of the books listed, but then I saw this one. The name Poppy Z. Brite sounded familiar, and I wasn't sure why until I realized it was because someone at the library had put a donated copy of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15320.Exquisite_Corpse' title='Exquisite Corpse by Poppy Z. Brite' rel='nofollow noopener'>Exquisite Corpse</a> in my box. Anyway, I read that <i>Lost Souls</i> "popularized the Splatterpunk subgenre, graphically violent, disturbing horror, infused with hip hop culture and gore." When</span>
  <span id="freeText4255786451644418238" style="display:none">I found out about this book from the "Getting Up to Speed in Horror" list on the NoveList database. I'd read or heard of most of the books listed, but then I saw this one. The name Poppy Z. Brite sounded familiar, and I wasn't sure why until I realized it was because someone at the library had put a donated copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15320.Exquisite_Corpse" title="Exquisite Corpse by Poppy Z. Brite" rel="nofollow noopener">Exquisite Corpse</a> in my box. Anyway, I read that <i>Lost Souls</i> "popularized the Splatterpunk subgenre, graphically violent, disturbing horror, infused with hip hop culture and gore." When I further investigated, I found that the book was about vampires, so I requested it immediately.<br /><br />Maybe it was because it took place in New Orleans, or maybe it was the lush, poetic writing, but <i>Lost Souls</i> brought me back to the world of Anne Rice's vampires. This was quite a bit more graphic than <i>The Vampire Chronicles</i>, but just as beautiful. <br /><br />The story begins as three threads which are then woven into one. First is the story of Christian, a 350+ year old vampire who tends bar in New Orleans and three vampires, Zillah, Molochai, and Twig, considered young and reckless by Christian, who live like nomads, hang out at bars filled with music, and who kill recklessly. The second is that of Nothing, a son conceived on one reckless night by Zillah, who Christian leaves on a doorstep and who grows up knowing nothing of what he really is. The third is that of Steven and Ghost, who comprise a band called Lost Souls? - Steve is a drunk who can't get over his ex-girlfriend Ann, and Ghost can see glimpses of the future. <br /><br />I was completely taken in by this world. It was like a mix between the poetic style of Francesca Lia Block and the graphic violence of Chuck Palahniuk or Bret Easton Ellis. I did finish this wishing there was something more... a sequel, perhaps...</span>
  <a data-text-id="4255786451644418238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HymQEPTMbD8vMHEWvGXJZATWEGeTRRlUXiPGSPdvdoUlD/nCT5KlV4gbxXdLkMO70on3r13IlzMFXYD5OiyEHw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('le1Wpcxq9lovo302SgjlIPRV5o2tG8cB94P/bk9lx9+vyz93dzQ/MoiIyVe9/e//IgoBRWOWSWas/bnfgiY1RQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/9558.Poppy_Z_Brite">About Poppy Z. Brite</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/9558.Poppy_Z_Brite"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1311937607p3/9558.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/9558.Poppy_Z_Brite">Poppy Z. Brite
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,773
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12033108728199368581">Poppy Z. Brite (born Melissa Ann Brite, now going by Billy Martin) is an American author born in New Orleans, Louisiana.<br/><br/>Born a biological female, Brite has written and talked much about his gender dysphoria/gender identity issues. He self-identifies almost completely as a homosexual male rather than female, and as of 2011 has started taking testosterone injections. His male name is Billy Martin.<br/><br/>He</span>
  <span id="freeText12033108728199368581" style="display:none">Poppy Z. Brite (born Melissa Ann Brite, now going by Billy Martin) is an American author born in New Orleans, Louisiana.<br /><br />Born a biological female, Brite has written and talked much about his gender dysphoria/gender identity issues. He self-identifies almost completely as a homosexual male rather than female, and as of 2011 has started taking testosterone injections. His male name is Billy Martin.<br /><br />He lived in Chapel Hill, North Carolina and Athens, Georgia prior to returning to New Orleans in 1993. He loves UNC basketball and is a sometime season ticket holder for the NBA, but he saves his greatest affection for his hometown football team, the New Orleans Saints.<br /><br />Brite and husband Chris DeBarr, a chef, run a de facto cat rescue and have, at any given time, between fifteen and twenty cats. Photos of the various felines are available on the "Cats" page of Brite's website. They have been known to have a few dogs and perhaps a snake as well in the menagerie. They are no longer together.<br /><br />During Hurricane Katrina in 2005, Brite at first opted to stay at home, but he eventually abandoned New Orleans and his cats and relocated 80 miles away to his mother's home in Mississippi. He used his blog to update his fans regarding the situation, including the unknown status of his house and many of his pets, and in October 2005 became one of the first 70,000 New Orleanians to begin repopulating the city.<br /><br />In the following months, Brite has been an outspoken and sometimes harsh critic of those who are leaving New Orleans for good. He was quoted in the <i>New York Times</i> and elsewhere as saying, in reference to those considering leaving, "If you’re ever lucky enough to belong somewhere, if a place takes you in and you take it into yourself, you don't desert it just because it can kill you. There are things more valuable than life."</span>
  <a data-text-id="12033108728199368581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
